1895-09-12 00:00:00 Scene 0 --- Participants: ['Aiden Riversong', 'Magnus Mulberrylane']
    Event statement
  • Aiden Riversong -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Aiden Riversong is trying to buy some fruit from Magnus Mulberrylane. They are negotiating a price. Aiden Riversong can sell the fruit for 6 coins back in her home town.
    Magnus Mulberrylane -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Magnus Mulberrylane is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Aiden Riversong. It costs Magnus Mulberrylane 2 coin to buy the fruit from the farm.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

          [25 Jul 1849 00:00:00]
          [25 Jul 1852 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 6 years old, he stumbled upon a hidden grove of wild peaches behind his family's orchard. He spent hours amongst the trees, lost in a world of sweet scent and dappled sunlight, feeling a connection to the earth and its bounty that he couldn't explain. Aiden knew, even then, that these peaches were special, different from the ones his father grew.
          [25 Jul 1856 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 9 years old, his father took him to the bustling market square for the first time. Aiden was captivated by the vibrant colors, the cacophony of sounds, and the endless stream of people bartering and trading. He watched, wide-eyed, as his father haggled over the price of apples, his voice booming with confidence and his face alight with a mischievous glint.
          [25 Jul 1859 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 13 years old, he overheard a group of older boys mocking a traveling storyteller for his fantastical tales. Aiden, who had always been drawn to stories and the magic they held, felt a surge of anger and protectiveness. He stood up for the storyteller, defending his right to share his tales, and surprised himself with the conviction in his voice.
          [25 Jul 1862 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 16 years old, he saved his meager earnings to buy a small plot of land on the outskirts of the village. He planted a single peach tree, the same variety he had found in the hidden grove years ago. He tended to it with meticulous care, whispering his hopes and dreams into the soil, and watched with pride as it grew strong and healthy.
          [25 Jul 1864 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 19 years old, he packed a small bag with his father's old compass and a handful of peaches from his own tree. He left a note for his family, explaining that he needed to find his own path, and set off into the world. He felt a mixture of fear and excitement as he walked away from the only life he had ever known, his heart pounding with the promise of adventure.
          [25 Jul 1866 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 21 years old, he arrived in a bustling city, his fruit stand set up in a crowded marketplace. He quickly learned the art of persuasion, using his charm and wit to draw in customers and sell his peaches at a good price. He made connections with other merchants, learning their trade secrets and expanding his knowledge of the world beyond his village.

  • Game Master's chain of thought
      Chain
    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master.     • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master.   • Aiden Riversong -- premise: Dewdrops clung to the colorful fruits displayed in the market of Fruitville, reflecting the soft morning light. The air buzzed with anticipation as traders and customers alike gathered for the day's trade. Aiden Riversong is trying to buy some fruit from Hazel Nutgrove. They are negotiating a price. Aiden Riversong can sell the fruit for 5 coins back in her home town.
    Hazel Nutgrove -- premise: Dewdrops clung to the colorful fruits displayed in the market of Fruitville, reflecting the soft morning light. The air buzzed with anticipation as traders and customers alike gathered for the day's trade. Hazel Nutgrove is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Aiden Riversong. It costs Hazel Nutgrove 1 coin to buy the fruit from the farm.

1895-09-13 00:00:00 Aiden Riversong -- Aiden Riversong -- "Four coins a basket, Hazel. That's a fair price for these fine fruits.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

          [25 Jul 1862 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 16 years old, he saved his meager earnings to buy a small plot of land on the outskirts of the village. He planted a single peach tree, the same variety he had found in the hidden grove years ago. He tended to it with meticulous care, whispering his hopes and dreams into the soil, and watched with pride as it grew strong and healthy.
          [25 Jul 1864 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 19 years old, he packed a small bag with his father's old compass and a handful of peaches from his own tree. He left a note for his family, explaining that he needed to find his own path, and set off into the world. He felt a mixture of fear and excitement as he walked away from the only life he had ever known, his heart pounding with the promise of adventure.
          [25 Jul 1866 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 21 years old, he arrived in a bustling city, his fruit stand set up in a crowded marketplace. He quickly learned the art of persuasion, using his charm and wit to draw in customers and sell his peaches at a good price. He made connections with other merchants, learning their trade secrets and expanding his knowledge of the world beyond his village.
